(@claude, 2026-05-22, branch: refactor/issue-1422/god-app-blocknode)

- [#1408] Downgrade Sentrux from a hard gate to an advisory signal (ADR-042 Addendum 3). The Sentrux binary is not installable in many contributor and AI-agent execution environments (distributed as Rust source under the Claude marketplace; no prebuilt binary), so every source-/workflow-/architecture-/governance-touching PR was hitting `gate-record.sentrux.missing` at the local pre-push hook and at CI's workflow-gate, requiring an `admin-approved:ai-override` label purely for tooling reasons (worked example: PR #1406 shipped with the override label even though no `src/scistudio/` was touched). Two changes: (1) `src/scistudio/qa/governance/gate_record.py::validate_gate_record` no longer emits `gate-record.sentrux.missing` — missing, skipped, and unknown sentrux evidence are all allowed. The narrower `gate-record.sentrux.not-passing` finding is kept and tightened to fire only on recorded `status="fail"` (status="unknown" and status="skipped" no longer count) so the gate's remaining scope is the case it was actually designed for: a developer who ran sentrux, observed a real failure, and is pushing anyway. The override label and `--bypass-label` flag still work for justified exceptions. (2) `.github/workflows/workflow-gate.yml` calls `sentrux_gate.verify_free_tier_claims` unchanged but converts findings to `::warning::` annotations instead of adding them to the blocking reports list — the workflow-gate job never fails on sentrux alone, and reviewers read the advisories in PR check details. The supersession is narrow: only Addendum 1 §D1 (sentrux required as gate evidence) and §D5 (free-tier-honesty rule's blocking semantics) are affected. §D2 committed gate records, §D3 six-stage gate, §D7 implementation tests required, §D8 legacy gate removal, §D9 generated artifacts, §D10 AI gate CLI requirement, and §D11/§D12 architecture frontmatter / drift checks are unaffected. The Sentrux tool, `SentruxEvidence` data model, `gate_record sentrux` CLI subcommand, `verify_free_tier_claims`, and `.sentrux/rules.toml` all continue to exist; only the enforcement is downgraded. Tests reflect the inverted semantics: `tests/qa/test_gate_record_ci.py::test_sentrux_required_for_applicable_changes` renamed to `test_sentrux_missing_evidence_is_allowed_for_applicable_changes` (asserts missing does NOT block); two new tests `test_sentrux_skipped_evidence_is_allowed_for_applicable_changes` and `test_sentrux_recorded_failure_still_blocks_locally` cover the new threshold. Existing `test_sentrux_evidence_rejects_*` tests in `tests/qa/test_gate_record.py` retained unchanged because the `SentruxEvidence` validation model itself is unchanged (Pro-required claims and impossible rule counts still rejected at parse time). (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: feat/sentrux-advisory)
### Fixed

- [#1376 #889 #1487] Three small bugfixes batched in one owner-authorised PR alongside enhancement #827. **(1) #1376 — `_on_cancel_block` state-machine guard** (`src/scistudio/engine/scheduler/_events.py`). Pre-fix the handler unconditionally set `BlockState.CANCELLED` for any known `block_id`, contradicting the architecture state table in `docs/architecture/ARCHITECTURE.md` §5.2 (which permits `CANCELLED` only from `RUNNING`/`PAUSED`). The handler now early-returns when `current_state` is anything other than `RUNNING`/`PAUSED` — `IDLE`/`READY` (no-op, workflow-level cancellation handles cleanup via `_on_cancel_workflow`'s separate `SKIPPED` branch), `DONE`/`ERROR`/`CANCELLED`/`SKIPPED` (no-op, terminal states are idempotent under cancel), unknown block id (silent no-op). The executable contract in `tests/engine/test_scheduler_state_machine_contract.py::test_cancel_block_state_table` had eight rows authored as the desired behaviour with six `xfail(strict=True)` markers documenting the drift; all six markers are removed now that the implementation matches. `tests/engine/test_scheduler_terminal_data.py` updates the existing `test_cancel_block_request_carries_block_type` test to seed `RUNNING` first (so it still exercises the `RUNNING → CANCELLED` path) and adds four new cases for IDLE-noop, READY-noop, terminal-state-noop (DONE/ERROR/SKIPPED), and unknown-block-id silence. **(2) #889 — `validate_connection` consumes effective ports per ADR-028 / ADR-029** (`src/scistudio/api/routes/blocks.py`, `src/scistudio/api/schemas.py`, `frontend/src/lib/api/blocks.ts`, `frontend/src/App.parts/useCanvasHandlers.ts`, `frontend/src/components/WorkflowCanvas.tsx`). `BlockConnectionValidation` grows two optional fields `source_node_config` and `target_node_config`; when present, the new helpers `_resolve_effective_output_port` / `_resolve_effective_input_port` instantiate the block via `BlockRegistryDep.instantiate(block_type, node_config)` and look the named port up against `Block.get_effective_*_ports()` — the same contract `BlockNode.tsx` already renders against. When absent, the route falls back to the existing static-spec path (legacy clients keep working). Registry failures (malformed config) demote to a debug-log + static fallback so the route never 500s. Frontend client now forwards `node.config` from both endpoints of the canvas edge; `useFlowEdges` in `WorkflowCanvas.tsx` now resolves the source port through `resolveVariadicPorts` (variadic AIBlock/CodeBlock/AppBlock — ports declared in `node.config.output_ports`) and then `computeEffectivePorts` (dynamic-port blocks like LoadData — `core_type` drives `accepted_types`) before computing the edge colour, ending the "canvas shows green when runtime would say red" UX gap called out in the audit. Five new backend tests in `tests/api/test_blocks.py` cover both the end-to-end LoadData(core_type=Array) → SaveData(core_type=Array) happy path, the core_type-mismatch reject, and three unit tests against the helpers themselves (output-side effective resolution, input-side, registry-failure fallback). Frontend `typeColorMap.test.ts` (new — see #1487 below) + the unchanged `BlockNode/ports.test.tsx`, `flowNodeBuilder.test.ts`, and `computeEffectivePorts.test.ts` suites continue to pass. **(3) #1487 — DataObject port/edge colour readable on white canvas** (`frontend/src/config/typeColorMap.ts`). `typeColorMap.DataObject` was `#e5e7eb` (Tailwind gray-200), nearly invisible on the white workflow canvas; every port that did not resolve to a more specific entry in the colour map (including the `resolveTypeColor()` fallback when `typeNames` is empty) rendered as gray-on-white. Changed to `#374151` (Tailwind gray-700) so DataObject stays visually distinct from the saturated typed-port palette while remaining legible. New `frontend/src/config/__tests__/typeColorMap.test.ts` locks the contract in via a relative-luminance assertion (Rec. 709 luminance < 0.5) plus full unit coverage of `resolveTypeColor` / `resolveRingColor` / `primaryTypeName` / `isAnyType` / `hashTypeName` (13 tests). (@claude, 2026-05-23, branch: fix/batch-1376-889-827-1487-20260523)

- [#1420 #1421] Retire the two real-bug waivers from the #1412 ESLint baseline. **#1420 (P1, `react-hooks/rules-of-hooks` on `frontend/src/components/nodes/BlockNode.tsx`)** — extract the default text-input branch of `InlineConfigField` into a new `InlineTextInputField` sub-component so its `useState` / `useRef` / `useLayoutEffect` calls sit at the top level of every component in the file. Pre-fix, those five Hooks ran only after the enum / boolean / number / textarea early returns, breaking the Hook order invariant; React would have surfaced "Rendered more hooks than during the previous render" the moment a single field ever toggled `ui_widget` (e.g. enum → string). Behavior is preserved exactly: the default text input still renders with the caret-preservation `useLayoutEffect`, the file_browser "..." button still opens the native dialog and falls back to the in-app modal on HTTP 500/non-ApiError, and the directory_browser still shows the clipboard-copy button. **#1421 (P2, `react-hooks/exhaustive-deps` on `frontend/src/App.tsx`)** — 10 dep gaps reconciled. Five workflow handlers (`saveWorkflow`, `saveWorkflowAs`, `runWorkflow`, `cancelWorkflow`, `refreshProjects`, `refreshBlocks`) are now `useCallback`-wrapped with full reactive dep lists so consumers downstream (keyboard-shortcut `useEffect` at L823, workflow autosave `useEffect` at L667) get stable identities and no longer churn on every render. The boot effect (`useEffect`, L656) is now a documented one-shot — kept on `[]` deps with an inline `eslint-disable-next-line react-hooks/exhaustive-deps` plus a comment explaining the `bootedRef` re-entry gate; running it more than once would double-load projects/blocks and clobber any in-flight error toast. The active-tab snapshot effect (L740) now correctly depends on `activeTabId` and `syncActiveTab` in addition to the workflow-state slices, so switching tabs also pushes the current snapshot (real correctness fix, not just a disable). The bottom-panel tab-change callback's bogus `activeBottomTab` dep is removed (the callback only reads its `tab` parameter, never the captured value). Two waiver blocks are deleted from `frontend/eslint.config.js`; every other waiver in the #1412 baseline (size, complexity, eqeqeq, unused-vars, type-imports, max-depth, ban-ts-comment) stays intact for the W2/W3/W4 follow-up waves. `frontend/src/__tests__/eslint-config.test.ts` is updated: the two "does NOT flag … (#1420 / #1421 waiver)" guards become positive `does flag … (waiver retired)` assertions so a regression that re-introduces either kind of bug now lint-fails on these exact paths. New `frontend/src/components/nodes/BlockNode.test.tsx` describe block exercises the extracted `InlineTextInputField` in all three branches (no widget → plain input, `file_browser` → Browse button only, `directory_browser` → Browse + clipboard); 481 vitest cases still pass (3 new). `npm run lint` reports 0 errors (down from 15 with waivers off) and 47 unchanged pre-existing warnings; typecheck / format / build clean. (@claude, 2026-05-22, branch: fix/issue-1420-1421/hooks-order)

- [#1400] Three-part hotfix landing the Git tab top-toolbar Diff/Restore UX gap reported post-#1364, plus two related canvas-refresh fixes for the Lineage Restore flow. **(1) Top-toolbar Diff/Restore (`frontend/src/components/Git/GitHistoryList.tsx`)** — adds `[Diff]` and `[Restore]` buttons next to `[Refresh]`, working in BOTH Graph and List views. Per-row List view buttons stay as redundant convenience. The buttons act on a shared `selectedCommit` state lifted into `GitHistoryList`; graph-dot clicks and list-row clicks both populate the selection, the buttons disable when nothing is selected, and a small `(short_sha)` indicator shows the active target. Pre-fix the buttons only existed per-row in List view per ADR-039 Addendum 1 §11.3 / #1355 — Graph view (the default) had no surfaces to invoke them, contradicting the spec intent. **(2) Lineage Restore canvas refresh (`frontend/src/components/Lineage/RunDetail.tsx`)** — `<RestoreWorkflowButton run={run} />` at line 484 now passes an explicit `onRestored` callback that fetches the freshly-restored workflow and either replaces the canvas in place (if the same workflow is open) or `openTab`s it (if not). Pre-fix the button's `onRestored` documentation already promised "the parent can refresh the canvas + GitStatusBadge", but the call site forgot to wire it — so `gitRestore` rewrote the YAML on disk but the canvas kept showing the in-memory snapshot from before the restore. **(3) Watchdog delete-then-create race (`frontend/src/hooks/useWebSocket.ts`)** — the WS `workflow.changed` handler now probes the file via `api.getWorkflow(id)` before clearing the canvas on `deleted`/`moved` events. On Windows, `git checkout` (and other atomic file replacements) sometimes emits a transient `deleted` event microseconds before the `created` event lands, which used to clear the canvas and surface the "Workflow 'X' was deleted on disk; canvas cleared" warning even though the file was actually present with the just-restored content. The probe trades 1 extra `getWorkflow` HTTP per `deleted` event (5-15ms, only triggered by `workflow.changed` events for the currently-loaded workflow — typically zero in steady state) for not nuking the canvas during the race. Genuinely-deleted files still clear the canvas with the legacy warning (probe fails → catch block runs the old path). This is a tactical patch for the symptom; the architectural root-cause fix is tracked in #1401 (workflow state version-vector contract). 14 + 23 = 37 vitest cases pass; 8 new tests cover the top-toolbar selection wiring, the lineage refresh delegation, the transient-delete-race regression, and the genuine-delete fallback. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: hotfix/git-tab-top-toolbar-diff-restore)

- [#1343 #1365] Restore the project/user drop-in `DataObject` runtime resolution contract end-to-end. **#1343 (already merged on `origin/main` as part of PR #1330; covered here by a regression test):** `TypeRegistry._scan_filesystem_dirs` now registers each loaded drop-in module in `sys.modules[spec.name]` *before* calling `spec.loader.exec_module(module)`, so the synthetic `_scistudio_type_dropin_*` name recorded in `TypeSpec.module_path` is resolvable by `importlib.import_module(...)`. Without this, every drop-in type was registerable but un-loadable — both the legacy `TypeRegistry.load_class(name)` path and the ADR-027 D11 `resolve(type_chain)` path raised `ModuleNotFoundError`. New regression test `tests/core/test_type_registry_scan_dirs.py::TestAddScanDir::test_drop_in_load_class_round_trip` exercises the full `scan_all → load_class → resolve(type_chain)` round-trip. **#1365 (this PR):** `scistudio.core.types.serialization._get_type_registry` — the worker-side singleton — now wires the same `<project>/types` + `~/.scistudio/types` scan dirs that `ApiRuntime.refresh_type_registry` wires for the API path, discovering the active project root via the `SCISTUDIO_PROJECT_DIR` env var (same contract as `scistudio.cli.mcp_bridge` and the agent provisioning layer). `LocalRunner.run` propagates `config['project_dir']` into the worker subprocess env as `SCISTUDIO_PROJECT_DIR` so the worker singleton can find the project root without needing the FastAPI runtime in-process. Without this, a workflow using a drop-in `DataObject` subclass under `<project>/types` resolved correctly on the API side but the worker subprocess silently fell back to base `DataObject` during reconstruction. Three regression tests in new `tests/engine/test_worker_reconstruction_scan_dirs.py` cover the singleton scan-dir wiring (project dir from env, user-wide always, empty env treated as unset, end-to-end `_reconstruct_one` returning the concrete drop-in class) plus `LocalRunner` env propagation. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-1343-1365/types-registry-worker-reconstruction)
- [#902 #1369] Two unrelated UX/CI bugfixes batched in one PR against `umbrella/2026-05-21-bug-sweep`. **(1) #902** — `CompletionWatcher.wait()` in `src/scistudio/blocks/ai/completion.py` now treats empty- or whitespace-only MCP signal reads as "file mid-write" and retries on the next poll instead of raising the spurious `ValueError("malformed MCP signal")`. Root cause: any writer that opens the signal file with mode `"w"` truncates it to 0 bytes before the JSON content lands; if the 250ms watcher poll lands inside that truncate window, `mcp_path.read_text()` returns `""` and `json.loads("")` raises `JSONDecodeError`. Production agents already use atomic `tempfile`+`os.replace` writes (#962/#909) and the test `StubAgent` fixture matched that pattern (`tests/blocks/ai/conftest.py::_atomic_write_signal`), but the reader-side hardening guards any third-party MCP writer that may not be atomic. Persistent malformed JSON (non-empty but invalid) still raises `ValueError` as before; the deadline still elapses to `TimeoutError` if the file never gets a valid payload. Refactors `test_non_atomic_writer_loses_race` to `test_non_atomic_writer_eventually_completes` in `tests/blocks/ai/test_completion_race.py` — the test now drives the same non-atomic-writer race window but asserts the watcher tolerates it and returns the `MCP_FINISH_TOOL` event once JSON lands (was: assert `ValueError`). Adds three new cases to `tests/blocks/ai/test_completion_skeleton.py`: empty signal → `TimeoutError` (not `ValueError`), whitespace-only signal → same, and empty → later valid JSON → watcher completes cleanly. **(2) #1369** — `SaveImage` in `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/src/scistudio_blocks_imaging/io/save_image.py` now re-declares the `path` config field directly in its own `config_schema.properties` (instead of inheriting from `IOBlock` via ADR-030 MRO merge), pinning `ui_widget="file_browser"`. The ADR-030 registry post-processor (`scistudio.blocks.registry._merge_config_schema`) auto-rewrites `path` to `directory_browser` for any `direction=="output"` IOBlock subclass that doesn't declare `path` locally; this default makes sense for `SaveData` (writes a directory) but contradicted `SaveImage.save()` → `_write_single()` which expects a concrete file path for single-image outputs (`out.tif`, `out.zarr`, `out.png`, `out.jpg`). The bottom panel's native dialog mapping (`frontend/src/components/BottomPanel.tsx::ui_widget` → `browseMode`) reads `file_browser` → `"file"` and `directory_browser` → `"directory"` directly, so a backend declaration is sufficient to fix the UX contract end-to-end without frontend changes. Adds `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/tests/test_save_image_browse_mode.py` with 4 cases: SaveImage's merged `path.ui_widget` is `file_browser`, `path.type` is single-string (no `items` key), `path` remains in `required`, and a regression guard asserting `SaveData.path.ui_widget` still resolves to `directory_browser` so the local override stays SaveImage-specific. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-902-1369/completion-saveimg)
- [#902 #1369] Two unrelated UX/CI bugfixes batched in one PR against `umbrella/2026-05-21-bug-sweep`. Codex P2 reconciliation also extends #1369 to fix a related batch-mode silent filename drop surfaced by the new file-browser UX. **(1) #902** — `CompletionWatcher.wait()` in `src/scistudio/blocks/ai/completion.py` now treats empty- or whitespace-only MCP signal reads as "file mid-write" and retries on the next poll instead of raising the spurious `ValueError("malformed MCP signal")`. Root cause: any writer that opens the signal file with mode `"w"` truncates it to 0 bytes before the JSON content lands; if the 250ms watcher poll lands inside that truncate window, `mcp_path.read_text()` returns `""` and `json.loads("")` raises `JSONDecodeError`. Production agents already use atomic `tempfile`+`os.replace` writes (#962/#909) and the test `StubAgent` fixture matched that pattern (`tests/blocks/ai/conftest.py::_atomic_write_signal`), but the reader-side hardening guards any third-party MCP writer that may not be atomic. Persistent malformed JSON (non-empty but invalid) still raises `ValueError` as before; the deadline still elapses to `TimeoutError` if the file never gets a valid payload. Refactors `test_non_atomic_writer_loses_race` to `test_non_atomic_writer_eventually_completes` in `tests/blocks/ai/test_completion_race.py` — the test now drives the same non-atomic-writer race window but asserts the watcher tolerates it and returns the `MCP_FINISH_TOOL` event once JSON lands (was: assert `ValueError`). Adds three new cases to `tests/blocks/ai/test_completion_skeleton.py`: empty signal → `TimeoutError` (not `ValueError`), whitespace-only signal → same, and empty → later valid JSON → watcher completes cleanly. **(2) #1369** — `SaveImage` in `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/src/scistudio_blocks_imaging/io/save_image.py` now re-declares the `path` config field directly in its own `config_schema.properties` (instead of inheriting from `IOBlock` via ADR-030 MRO merge), pinning `ui_widget="file_browser"`. The ADR-030 registry post-processor (`scistudio.blocks.registry._merge_config_schema`) auto-rewrites `path` to `directory_browser` for any `direction=="output"` IOBlock subclass that doesn't declare `path` locally; this default makes sense for `SaveData` (writes a directory) but contradicted `SaveImage.save()` → `_write_single()` which expects a concrete file path for single-image outputs (`out.tif`, `out.zarr`, `out.png`, `out.jpg`). The bottom panel's native dialog mapping (`frontend/src/components/BottomPanel.tsx::ui_widget` → `browseMode`) reads `file_browser` → `"file"` and `directory_browser` → `"directory"` directly, so a backend declaration is sufficient to fix the UX contract end-to-end without frontend changes. Adds `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/tests/test_save_image_browse_mode.py` with 6 cases: SaveImage's merged `path.ui_widget` is `file_browser`, `path.type` is single-string (no `items` key), `path` remains in `required`, a regression guard asserting `SaveData.path.ui_widget` still resolves to `directory_browser` so the local override stays SaveImage-specific, plus two batch-mode regressions (file-suffix path → honours stem as filename prefix, bare-directory path → preserves legacy `image_XXXX` prefix). **(3) Codex P2 reconciliation (PR #1395 review)** — Codex flagged that consistently exposing `ui_widget="file_browser"` creates a UI/runtime mismatch for batch SaveImage saves: a user typing `out.tif` for a node that turns out to receive a multi-item `Collection` at runtime would have their filename silently dropped (pre-fix batch logic did `out_dir = path if path.suffix == "" else path.parent` then wrote `out_dir/image_0000.tif`). The companion runtime fix in `SaveImage.save()` now branches on `path.suffix`: paths with a file suffix use `path.parent` as `out_dir` and `path.stem` as the per-item filename prefix (`out.tif` + 3 items → `out_0000.tif`, `out_0001.tif`, `out_0002.tif`); paths without a suffix preserve the legacy bare-directory branch (`path` is `out_dir`, default `image` prefix), keeping every existing workflow YAML unchanged. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-902-1369/completion-saveimg)

### Added

- [#1360] Add `scripts/scistudio_pr_create.py`: a wrapper around `gh pr create` that pre-flights `python -m scistudio.qa.governance.gate_record ci` locally with the real PR body before invoking GitHub. Motivated by PR #1351's 4-round CI fix cycle (each round surfaced a different gate-record gap that local `gate_record pre-push` does NOT catch: `pre-push` runs only structural `validate_gate_record`, while CI's `Verify Workflow Compliance` runs the full guard orchestration). The wrapper filters findings that are structurally impossible to satisfy pre-PR: (a) findings under the three PR-state-dependent guards — `core_change_guard.*`, `pr_merge_guard.*`, `human_bypass_guard.*` — because their evidence (admin labels on the PR) cannot exist before the PR is created; (b) `gate-record.stage.not-done` for the `commit_and_submit_pr` stage specifically, because that stage is only marked done by `gate_record finalize` which itself requires the PR URL (a chicken-and-egg surfaced during dogfooding this very wrapper on PR #1360). CI remains the authoritative enforcer for the (a) subset. Hard-fails (exit 1) on any remaining findings (`docs_landing`, `issue_link`, `sentrux_gate`, `mod_guard`, `weakened_ci_check`, and `gate-record.stage.not-done` for any other stage) and prints a structured list with rule_id + severity + message so the author can fix locally before pushing. Supports `--dry-run` (preflight without `gh pr create`) and `SCISTUDIO_SKIP_PREFLIGHT=1` (escape hatch for emergencies; CI still gates). Updates `docs/ai-developer/specific_rules/gated-workflow.md` §3.7 to mark the wrapper as the preferred PR-creation entry for AI-authored work. 22 unit tests in `tests/scripts/test_scistudio_pr_create.py` cover `extract_body` (4 cases for space/equals/file/missing variants plus a special-chars round-trip), `find_gate_record` (6 cases including umbrella-PR multi-record disambiguation per #1340 manager-task-kind tie-break + malformed-JSON skip), `filter_findings` (8 cases: all-filtered / none-filtered / mixed / empty / missing-key / missing-rule-id / commit_and_submit_pr stage filtered / other-stage stays), and `main()` smoke (help + dry-run with skip-preflight). Does NOT modify `src/scistudio/qa/governance/gate_record.py` (protected core; out of scope for this issue per ADR-042). (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: feat/issue-1360/pr-create-wrapper)

### Fixed

- [#1356] ADR-039 Addendum 1 §11.4 branch-delete orphan guard (option C silent auto-tag). Before `DELETE /api/git/branches/{name}` runs `git branch -d|-D`, the endpoint computes `engine.commits_reachable_only_from(name)` (via `git rev-list <branch> --not <all-other-refs>`), intersects the result with `runs.workflow_git_commit` via the new `LineageStore.workflow_git_commits_in(sha_list)` query, and creates one `refs/scistudio/lineage/<sha>` ref per lineage-referenced orphan via `git update-ref` so those commits stay reachable after the delete. Per owner decision 2026-05-21 this is intentionally silent — no warn / confirm dialog change, no response payload change; the existing `window.confirm` in `BranchPicker.tsx::handleDelete` is untouched. The ref namespace `refs/scistudio/lineage/*` is deliberately outside `refs/tags/*` so the History view's chip renderer (which scans `refs/tags/` per #1011 hotfix) does not surface them, and outside `refs/heads/*` so BranchPicker's branch list (which scans `refs/heads/` only) is unaffected. `engine.tag(name, sha)` uses `update-ref` internally (idempotent: overwrites on re-run) rather than `git tag` so the ref namespace is caller-controlled. The safety net is best-effort: when `runtime.lineage_store` is not initialised the delete proceeds without the safety check (matches the rest of the lineage write path). Cleanup of accumulated `refs/scistudio/lineage/*` refs is deferred to #1380 with a `TODO(#1380)` comment in the new code. Tests: new `tests/core/test_lineage_store.py` covers `workflow_git_commits_in` (6 cases: intersection, empty input → empty set without SQL, absent SHAs filtered, NULL rows filtered, duplicates collapsed, return type is `set[str]`); `tests/core/test_git_engine.py` gains 6 new tests for `commits_reachable_only_from` + `tag` (A-B-C/A-B-D fixture → orphan = [D] only, merged branch → empty list, unknown branch → empty list, `tag` creates ref under namespace, `tag` is idempotent, `tag` stays out of `refs/tags/`, post-pin idempotency); `tests/api/test_git_endpoints.py::test_branch_delete_endpoint` rewritten to assert the tagged-orphan flow end-to-end via the FastAPI test client (force=true required because divergent feature branches are the precondition for orphan candidates), plus new `test_branch_delete_endpoint_no_lineage_reference_leaves_no_refs` and `test_branch_delete_endpoint_safety_net_keeps_sha_reachable` covering negative and reachability invariants. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: feat/issue-1356/branch-delete-orphan-guard)

- [#1389] `gate_record._is_test_path` now classifies vitest co-located tests as test paths. The pre-fix classifier only recognised pytest conventions (`tests/` prefix, `/tests/` substring, `test_*.py`, `*_test.py`), so a vitest-only PR like `frontend/src/components/PortEditorTable.test.tsx` was treated as touching an implementation file with no accompanying test change — triggering `gate-record.tests.changed-test-required` and forcing the author to either restructure tests or burn an `admin-approved:ai-override` label (worked examples: PRs #1383, #1299, #1313, #1320). The classifier now additionally accepts the `__tests__/` directory convention and a frozen `_VITEST_NAME_SUFFIXES` tuple covering `.test.{ts,tsx,js,jsx}` + `.spec.{ts,tsx,js,jsx}`. Both behaviours (filename suffix + `__tests__/` dir) are documented inline with a `#1389` reference and motivation. Gap 1 of #1389; Gap 2 (wrapper `--base` hardcoded to `origin/main`) was already closed by PR #1385. 26 new tests in `tests/qa/test_gate_record.py` (`TestIsTestPathPytestConventions`, `TestIsTestPathVitestRecognition`, `TestIsTestPathImplementationStays`, `TestVitestChangedTestPathAccepted`) cover pytest regression (6 cases), vitest suffix matrix (7 cases across `.test.tsx/.test.ts/.test.js/.spec.tsx/.spec.ts/.spec.jsx`), `__tests__/` directory matching (3 cases), implementation-stays regression (8 cases including `PortEditorTableHelper.ts` which would naively match a substring of `.test.tsx`), and end-to-end `GateRecord` schema acceptance of vitest paths in `changed_test_paths` plus continued rejection of non-test paths there.
- [#1366] Frontend `PortEditorTable` now clears `capability_id` when the user changes a port row's `types` or `extension`, preventing stale capability mismatches at workflow-validation time. `handleTypeChange` and `handleExtensionChange` previously preserved the existing `capability_id`, but the pinned capability is only registered for the previous `(direction, type, extension)` tuple — a user could save a workflow that looked valid in the editor and then fail backend validation because the old capability was no longer registered for the new tuple. Both change handlers now set `capability_id = null` after updating their respective columns; the row's `CapabilityDropdown` then re-renders empty and the user re-selects for the new tuple. Regression tests in `frontend/src/components/PortEditorTable.test.tsx` exercise both handlers (type change clears the id; extension change clears the id). One existing test (`normalises typed extensions: lowercases and strips leading dots`) updated to reflect that the row now carries `capability_id: null` after any extension edit — the row had no capability pinned to begin with, so the null is functionally neutral but the assertion shape changed. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-1366/port-capability-clear)
- [#1382] `scripts/scistudio_pr_create.py` now reads `--base` from the forwarded `gh pr create` argv and resolves it to the correct remote ref before invoking the pre-flight `gate_record ci`. Previously the wrapper always defaulted to `--base origin/main`, so any sub-PR targeting a non-main base (most commonly an umbrella branch from a coordinated dispatch) saw the parent branch's commits included in the diff against `origin/main`. Those parent commits — manager checklist + manager gate record + audit JSON — are not in the child agent's `scope.include`, so `gate_record ci` reported false `gate-record.scope.outside-include` findings and the agent had to fall back to `SCISTUDIO_SKIP_PREFLIGHT=1` (ADR-042 §3.7-documented emergency escape) to open the PR. New helpers `extract_base()` (mirrors `extract_body()` argv parsing) and `resolve_base_ref()` (maps a plain branch name to `origin/<name>`; preserves already-qualified `origin/*` or `refs/*` refs verbatim; defaults to `origin/main` when `--base` is absent). The fix is content-agnostic — makes zero assumptions about whether the base is `main`, an umbrella branch, a release branch, or a feature stack. 8 new tests in `tests/scripts/test_scistudio_pr_create.py` (`TestExtractBase`, `TestResolveBaseRef`, `TestMainBaseWiring`) cover argv parsing edge cases (space/equals/missing/twice/substring-non-match), all base-resolution branches (None default, plain prefixing, already-qualified passthrough, `refs/` passthrough, deliberately non-umbrella branch names), and `main()` integration confirming the resolved base actually threads into `run_gate_record_ci`. Discovered during umbrella PR #1377 W1 dispatch (`fix/bug-sweep-2026-05-21/tier1-surgical` → `umbrella/2026-05-21-bug-sweep`).
- [#1367 #1370] Two DAGScheduler lifecycle bugs in `src/scistudio/engine/scheduler.py`. (1) #1367 — `resume()`, `rerun_block()`, and `reset_block()` previously flipped `BlockState.READY` without calling `_emit_block_ready()`, so frontend WS subscribers missed readiness events whenever the scheduler re-dispatched a block outside the initial execute path. `BLOCK_READY` is now emitted exactly once per scheduler-owned IDLE→READY transition. New `TestSchedulerLifecycleBlockReady` in `tests/engine/test_scheduler.py` exercises all three paths. (2) #1370 — `_run_interactive()` stored the interactive block's result directly, bypassing the ADR-020 §3 collection-output normalization that `_run_and_finalize()` and the worker-subprocess path apply via `scistudio.engine.runners.worker._normalize_outputs`. A custom interactive block returning a bare `DataObject` or `list[DataObject]` on an `is_collection=True` port now goes through the same `_normalize_outputs` call before the result lands in `_block_outputs`. New `tests/engine/test_scheduler_interactive.py` covers both shapes. (@claude, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-1367-1370/scheduler-emit-normalize)
- [#1109 #1309] Two block-IO contract bugs surfaced during the 2026-05-21 bug sweep. **#1109 — `BlockRegistry.find_loader` / `find_saver` compound-extension fallback:** `_ext_in_mapping` did exact-key compare against `supported_extensions`, but the documented contract (and the existing `IOBlock._detect_format` behaviour) is compound-first matching with single-suffix fallback. Queries like `.ome.tif` silently missed loaders declaring only `.tif`. Introduces a shared `_iter_compound_to_single_suffix` helper that produces the suffix chain (`.ome.tif → [".ome.tif", ".tif"]`, `.foo.bar.baz → [".foo.bar.baz", ".bar.baz", ".baz"]`) and threads it through `_ext_in_mapping`, the ADR-043 `list_format_capabilities` extension filter, `_capability_satisfies_query`, and `_matching_capabilities_for_legacy_io` so the legacy `find_*` path and the new capability lookup agree. Regression tests in `tests/blocks/test_registry_find.py::TestCompoundExtensionFallback` cover the fallback (`.ome.tif → .tif`), explicit-compound preference (`.ome.tif → .ome.tif` when both registered), the dtype-None code path (extension-only callers), the three-segment walk (`.foo.bar.tif → .tif`), the exact-match regression, and the symmetric `find_saver` case. **#1309 — CodeBlock notebook + python backends honor `working_directory`:** ADR-041 §4 promises CodeBlock cwd = `working_directory` (default `"."` = project root) so notebooks and scripts can read project-relative paths like `Path("data/raw")`. Both backends hard-coded `cwd=context.exchange_dir`, so the subprocess (and, for the notebook backend, `--ExecutePreprocessor.cwd=...`) ran from the per-run exchange dir under `<project>/exchange/codeblock-…/<run-id>/`. The fix computes `script_cwd = context.config.resolve_working_directory(context.project_dir)` once in each backend's `run()` (and again in `notebook.resolve()` so `ResolvedInterpreter.working_directory` and the nbconvert kernel cwd agree) and passes it as the subprocess cwd. The exchange dir remains the materialisation target for declared input/output ports; only the *executing* process cwd changes. New `tests/blocks/code/test_codeblock_backends.py` covers both backends with the default `working_directory='.'` and a custom subdir, asserting the captured subprocess cwd equals `resolve_working_directory(project_dir)` and is **not** the exchange dir. Two existing integration tests (`test_codeblock_notebooks.py::test_codeblock_runs_notebook_and_collects_typed_output_plus_executed_artifact`, sibling `test_failed_notebook_retains_executed_artifact_file_when_nbconvert_created_it`, plus `test_codeblock_execution.py::test_codeblock_runs_python_script_through_exchange`) encoded the buggy cwd in their fixture scripts (e.g. `Path("outputs/summary/result.txt")` worked only because the subprocess ran from `<exchange_dir>`); these are updated to write to the per-run exchange-outputs folder via an absolute path computed from the deterministic `<exchange_root>/codeblock-<block_id>/<run_id>/outputs` layout. **Out of scope (filed for follow-up):** the matlab, r_quarto, and shell backends share the same hard-coded `cwd=context.exchange_dir` shape and likely have the same bug, but #1309's reproduction path covers only notebook + python; a follow-up should sweep the remaining backends. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-1109-1309/registry-codeblock-cwd)

- [#1306 #1371] ADR-043 imaging metadata fidelity — capability declarations now match handler behaviour. (1) #1306 regression coverage: `LoadImage._load_tiff` was already wired (PR #1304) to parse OME-XML from the TIFF `ImageDescription` tag via `tifffile.TiffFile.ome_metadata` + `ome_types.from_xml`, but the only existing regression was the SaveImage→LoadImage round-trip; this PR adds `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/tests/test_load_image_ome.py` exercising the externally-authored OME-TIFF load path that #1306 cites (write OME-XML directly via `tifffile.imwrite(description=...)`, assert `image.meta.ome.images[0].pixels.physical_size_x` matches the source), plus a plain-TIFF negative (no OME-XML → `meta.ome is None`) and a malformed-OME defensive fallback. (2) #1371 capability declarations: `LoadImage` / `SaveImage` zarr capabilities drop to `level="pixel_only"` because `_load_zarr` / `_write_zarr` round-trip array data + the `axes` group attribute only — never OME, never typed `Image.Meta` fields. PNG / JPEG declarations narrow `format_metadata_{reads,writes}` from the broad `"ome"` token to the precise hierarchical OME field paths actually persisted (`ome.pixels.physical_size_x` / `ome.pixels.physical_size_y`, the only fields Pillow's EXIF DPI round-trip preserves). TIFF stays on the broad `"ome"` token — its writer / loader genuinely round-trip the full OME-XML. (3) #1371 frontend matching: `frontend/src/api/capabilities.ts::lossyOmeFields` previously exact-matched flattened source paths (e.g. `pixels.physical_size_x`) against declarations (e.g. the literal `"ome"`), producing false positives for TIFF (broad `"ome"` declaration → every source field flagged as dropped) and false negatives once #1371's narrowed declarations landed. The matcher now treats `"ome"` as a prefix covering every OME source path and strips the `ome.` prefix from hierarchical declarations before comparison. Test coverage: `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/tests/test_save_image_capabilities.py` (zarr round-trip preserves `meta.ome is None`; PNG round-trip preserves only `physical_size_x/y` per the narrowed declaration; capability-declaration assertions guard against re-introducing the broad `"ome"` overclaim); updated existing assertions in `test_format_capabilities.py` and the `LossySaveWarning` / `adr043-a3-smoke` vitest suites to match the new fidelity contract. Out of scope per #1306 §Acceptance.3: ImageJ TIFF `unit`/`spacing` → OME `physical_size_*` mapping (separate enhancement). (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-1306-1371/imaging-ome-fidelity)
- [#1110 #617 #1281 #1282 #1368] Tier 1 surgical bug-sweep (2026-05-21). Five independent ≤25-LOC root-cause fixes batched in one PR against `umbrella/2026-05-21-bug-sweep`: (1) **#1110** — advertise `.markdown` and `.htm` on the `SaveData` and `LoadData` `Text` (and `Artifact`-as-text) `FormatCapability` records and add `.markdown` / `.htm` to `_TEXT_FORMAT_MAP`. `_save_text` / `_load_text` already accepted both extensions but the registry-visible capability map did not, so `find_saver_capability(Text, '.markdown')` could not discover SaveData. Both directions are updated so the ADR-043 FR-001 / FR-002 Load ↔ Save mirror invariant asserted by `test_save_extension_map_mirrors_load` stays intact. (2) **#617** — escape `'` → `''` in `_native_dialog_windows` PowerShell-single-quoted strings via a new `_ps_single_quote_escape` helper, run through `initial_dir`, `default_filename`, and `file_filter` before interpolation. Workflow names like `Bob's run` no longer break the dialog script syntax. (3) **#1281** — key `CodeBlockExchangeManifest.ports` by `(direction, name)` tuple in `initialise_exchange_manifest` so a CodeBlock declaring an input port and an output port sharing a name (e.g. `data → data`) keeps both records; update the three in-file readers (`prepare_codeblock_exchange`, `discover_declared_outputs`'s `known_folders` build and per-port record lookup) accordingly, and serialise tuple keys as `"<direction>:<name>"` in `to_dict()` so JSON consumers see both records under distinct stable string keys. The one downstream test that asserted the old bare-name JSON shape is updated. (4) **#1282** — narrow `_is_codeblock_spec` in `src/scistudio/workflow/validator.py` from `spec.base_category == 'code'` to the concrete-CodeBlock identifiers (`name == "Code Block"`, `type_name == "code_block"`, or module-path + class-name == `scistudio.blocks.code.code_block.CodeBlock`). Custom or synthetic code-category specs no longer trigger CodeBlock v2 config validation and the spurious `script_path missing` / port-field errors that came with it. (5) **#1368** — replace `_make_block()` in `tests/blocks/app/test_appblock_fiji_integration.py` with the direct `AppBlock()` construction pattern matching `tests/blocks/test_app_block.py`, and drop the `BlockState` import. PR #1351 removed `Block.transition` and `BlockState` at the `Block` level, but the Fiji/AppBlock integration helper still called both, raising `AttributeError` at test collection time when Fiji is installed. Regression tests at `tests/blocks/io/test_save_data.py::TestRoundTripText` (parametrised `.markdown`/`.htm` round trip + capability-map shape assertion), `tests/blocks/io/test_load_data.py::test_extension_map_contains_markdown_and_htm_for_text`, `tests/api/test_filesystem_dialog.py` (6 cases — escape helper unit, save_file `initial_dir` / `default_filename` / `file_filter`, file-open `initial_dir`, `None` initial_dir), `tests/blocks/code/test_codeblock_exchange.py::test_initialise_manifest_keeps_same_named_input_and_output_ports` + `test_prepare_exchange_materialises_input_when_output_has_same_name`, and `tests/workflow/test_validator.py::TestIsCodeBlockSpecNarrowing` (4 cases). (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/bug-sweep-2026-05-21/tier1-surgical)

- [#1362] Centralise the `.workflow/records/**` exclusion across all governance modules in a shared `src/scistudio/qa/governance/paths.py::is_gate_record_path` helper, **and** fix the `docs_record` CLI so `--updated CHANGELOG.md` lands in the `changelog` class instead of being silently miscategorised as `docs`. Two related governance-routing bugs surfaced sequentially during PR #1359 CI debugging:

  **Bug A — `.workflow/records/**` records were treated as protected by three governance modules** that still consulted a raw `.workflow/**` glob without the records exception (`core_change_guard._is_protected`, `sentrux_gate.sentrux_applies_to_changes`, `docs_landing._requires_landing`, plus the gate-record-internal duplicate `gate_record._sentrux_applies`). The exception had been added in isolation twice already — `mod_guard.py` (#1316/#1317) and `gate_record.py::_is_governance_path` (#1340/#1346) — each pass missing the rest. Adds `src/scistudio/qa/governance/paths.py` with `GATE_RECORD_PATTERNS` and `is_gate_record_path(path)`; the four governance modules above now import the helper as the single source of truth. The module docstring explicitly tells future authors of new `.workflow/**` checks to call the helper.

  **Bug B — `docs_record` CLI silently routed `CHANGELOG.md` into the `docs` landing class**, leaving `changelog` always empty so every PR that genuinely updated `CHANGELOG.md` still failed `docs_landing.missing-changelog` and had to either N/A the changelog (untruthful — the file *was* updated) or bypass the workflow gate entirely via `admin-approved:ai-override` (the path PR #1346 took). Adds an explicit `_CHANGELOG_PATHS` frozenset and routes `CHANGELOG.md` into the `changelog` class in `docs_record`. After this fix, `gate_record docs --updated CHANGELOG.md` produces `docs_landing.changelog == {"paths": ["CHANGELOG.md"]}` as expected.

  Test coverage: `tests/qa/test_governance_paths.py` (now 6 test classes, 24 assertions) covers the helper itself, per-module records-exclusion regressions, and three `docs_record` changelog-routing scenarios (CHANGELOG.md → changelog; mixed paths → correct three-way split; no CHANGELOG → changelog stays empty). (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-1362/governance-records-helper)

- [#1334 #560] Remove the vestigial worker-side block state machine (`Block.state`, `Block._state`, `Block.transition`, `_VALID_TRANSITIONS`) so the engine-owned `DAGScheduler._block_states` is the single source of truth (ADR-018 §8.1). The vestigial code crashed AppBlock at first use: `worker.py` only transitioned `IDLE → READY` before calling `block.run()`, but `AppBlock.run()` called `self.transition(BlockState.PAUSED)` which required `RUNNING` per `_VALID_TRANSITIONS`, raising `RuntimeError: Invalid state transition: ready -> paused` on every AppBlock invocation. Replaces the cancellation signal with a typed `BlockCancelledByAppError` exception (new `src/scistudio/blocks/base/exceptions.py`); the worker catches it and emits `final_state="cancelled"` in the stdout envelope (same wire shape as before — `LocalRunner` translation into `BlockTerminalStateReportedError` and the `DAGScheduler` terminal-state recording path are untouched). Also strips the symmetrically-vestigial `AIBlock._safe_transition` helper and its 11 swallow-the-error call sites, removes the `READY` transition boilerplate from `SubWorkflowBlock._sequential_execute`, and updates ARCHITECTURE.md §5.2 to make the engine-ownership of the state machine explicit. ~10 test files cleaned: deletes the two state-machine classes from `tests/blocks/test_block_base.py`, strips `block.transition(BlockState.READY/RUNNING)` boilerplate from 6 other test files, rewires `tests/engine/test_worker.py::_CancellingStubBlock` to raise `BlockCancelledByAppError` (deletes the dead `_ErroringStubBlock` path), and updates the `tests/engine/test_scheduler.py` docstring for the new cancellation mechanism. Adds `TestAppBlockVestigialStateRemoval` regression class to `tests/blocks/test_app_block.py` with three assertions: AppBlock.run() does not crash on the originally-reported state precondition, `Block` exposes neither `state` nor `transition`, and `ProcessExitedWithoutOutputError` surfaces as `BlockCancelledByAppError`. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: fix/issue-1334-vestigial-block-state)

### Added

- [#1340] Wire `vulture` into `scistudio.qa.audit.full_audit` as an informational dead-code child report (`vulture_audit`) and fix three adjacent gate-workflow bugs surfaced while landing the PR. ADR-042 code-quality spec (`docs/specs/adr-042-code-quality-tools.md` lines 22 and 64) named vulture as a standard external tool but the repository never installed or invoked it; the 2026-05-21 architecture-consistency audit found `ResourceManager.acquire()` is defined-but-uncalled — exactly the dead-code class vulture catches. **(1) vulture wiring:** new `src/scistudio/qa/audit/vulture_audit.py` runs vulture in-process against `[tool.vulture]` paths and emits `Severity.WARNING` findings under the `vulture.dead-code` rule id; the child report status stays `pass` so it never sets `blocks_merge` in v1. Adds `vulture>=2.11` to `[project.optional-dependencies].dev`, `[tool.vulture]` config in `pyproject.toml`, a starter `vulture_allowlist.py` covering Pydantic/FastAPI/entry-point conventions, ruff `extend-exclude` for the allowlist file, and a `--skip-vulture` CLI flag on `full_audit`. Updates `docs/specs/adr-042-consistency-tools.md` `full_audit.run` signature contract to add `include_vulture: bool = True`. **(2) governance-touch rule fix:** `gate_record.py` previously treated every `.workflow/**` change as a governance touch, so every AI PR's own gate-record evidence file under `.workflow/records/<issue>-<slug>.json` tripped `gate-record.governance-touch.missing` and forced `governance_touch=true` for trivially-shaped PRs. Adds `_is_governance_path()` with `.workflow/records/**` exclusion (same pattern PR #1317 used in `mod_guard.py`). **(3) amend `--governance-touch` CLI flag:** the original `amend` CLI did not expose `governance_touch`, so the only way to set it on an in-flight gate record after legitimately bringing governance code into scope was direct JSON edit (caught by auto-mode classifier as evidence tampering). Adds the flag; `amend_record(governance_touch=True)` flips the field. **(6) honor `[tool.vulture]` from `pyproject.toml`:** the initial `vulture_audit` wired `[tool.vulture]` into `pyproject.toml` (paths, exclude, min_confidence, sort_by_size, ignore_decorators) but instantiated `Vulture(verbose=False, ignore_decorators=[], ignore_names=[])` with hard-coded empty lists and never called `scavenge(exclude=…)` — so the entire `[tool.vulture]` block was silent dead config. New `_load_pyproject_vulture_config()` reads `[tool.vulture]` via `tomllib`; `_run_vulture` passes `ignore_decorators`, `ignore_names`, and `exclude` through to the actual `Vulture()` instance and `scavenge()` call. The `check()` summary now exposes `pyproject_config_honored` so reviewers can see which config keys reached the scanner. 5 new tests in `tests/qa/test_audit_vulture.py` cover: missing pyproject → empty dict; tool.vulture table read correctly; malformed TOML tolerated; `ignore_decorators` actually suppresses decorated functions (with baseline vs honored comparison); `exclude` actually filters scavenged paths. Caught by Codex auto-review on PR #1346 as P2; reviewer's concern that FastAPI `@app.*` / `@router.*` handlers would surface as false positives once `min_confidence` is lowered is now structurally addressed. **(5) umbrella gate-record discovery:** the "exactly one gate record per PR" rule failed every umbrella PR because each sub-PR's merge into the umbrella brought its own gate record along, leaving N records in the diff when CI / `pr-ready` only expected 1. Discovery now detects the umbrella case by `task_kind`: when multiple records exist, prefer the one whose `task_kind == "manager"` (the umbrella manager's own record); sub-PR records pass through as historical evidence that already passed their own CI runs. Updated `_discover_gate_record` in `src/scistudio/qa/governance/gate_record.py` and the equivalent shell logic in `.github/workflows/workflow-gate.yml` (both the gate-record discovery step and the guard-orchestration step). Updated `docs/specs/adr-042-gate-record-sentrux-workflow.md` §5.5 step 3 to document the carve-out. 4 new tests in `tests/qa/test_gate_record.py` cover: single record returned unchanged, manager record picked on umbrella, multiple manager records → None (defensive), multiple non-manager records → None (fail closed). **(4) pre-push / pr-ready chicken-and-egg fix:** the gate validator required all six stages done at `pre-push` and `pr-ready`, but `commit_and_submit_pr` is only set by `finalize`, which requires a PR URL, which only exists after `gh pr create` — unsolvable without override labels. Adds `POST_PR_STAGES = {COMMIT_AND_SUBMIT_PR}` and a `require_post_pr_stages` parameter on `validate_gate_record`; `check_pre_push` and `check_pr_ready` set it to `False`. CI (`check_pr`) keeps the strict default. Updates `docs/specs/adr-042-gate-record-sentrux-workflow.md` §3.7 and `docs/adr/ADR-042-addendum1.md` §5 to describe the carve-out and the chicken-and-egg reasoning. Tests: `tests/qa/test_audit_vulture.py` (6 cases: vulture-missing → SKIPPED, nonexistent paths → pass with zero findings, real dead code → WARNING findings with confidence in `evidence`, allowlist suppression, `main()` exits 0 on warnings-only, `main()` exits 0 on skip); new cases in `tests/qa/test_gate_record.py` (3 governance-path cases, 2 amend `--governance-touch` cases, 3 chicken-and-egg cases covering pr-ready, ci, pre-push); `tests/qa/test_audit_full_audit.py` asserts the new vulture child appears in the markdown summary. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: feat/issue-1340/wire-vulture)

### Fixed

- [#1305 #1307 #1308] ADR-043 Phase D E2E hotfix round (owner authorized 2026-05-20). Three in-PR framework fixes plus E2E-001/E2E-002 evidence: (1) `LocalRunner.run` now passes `cwd=config['project_dir']` to `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec` so block subprocess workers inherit the active project root instead of the launcher cwd — without this, LoadImage(`data/raw/foo.tif`) and SaveData(`data/parquet/out.parquet`) silently resolve against wherever `scistudio gui` was launched, leaking files into the developer worktree and breaking any portable workflow. Regression tests at `tests/engine/test_local_runner.py::TestLocalRunnerWorkerCwd` (3 cases: project_dir set, missing, non-string). (2) `frontend/src/components/nodes/BlockNode.tsx` now filters the inline Format dropdown by the block's active `core_type` config when present, so a SaveData node with `core_type=Series` can never expose `core.dataframe.csv.save` or `imaging.image.png.save` as a selectable option — runtime behaviour on illegal `(core_type, capability_id)` combinations was previously undefined. Regression tests at `frontend/src/components/nodes/BlockNode.test.tsx` (3 cases: DataFrame filter, Series filter, no-core_type no-op). (3) `scistudio.blocks.code.code_block._persisted_codeblock_config` and `scistudio.blocks.code.validation._RUNTIME_ONLY_CONFIG_KEYS` now both strip `workflow_id` from the raw config before instantiating `CodeBlockConfig(extra="forbid")` — `DAGScheduler._build_enriched_config` injects `workflow_id` alongside `block_id` and `project_dir` at the block boundary, and the missing strip-set entry made every CodeBlock run inside a workflow fail with `pydantic extra_forbidden`. Regression test at `tests/blocks/code/test_codeblock_execution.py::test_persisted_codeblock_config_strips_engine_enrichment_fields`. Phase D evidence committed at `docs/audit/adr-043-package-migration-e2e-cases.md`: E2E-001 is partial-pass (all 17 nodes Done on the integrated umbrella branch after a workflow-domain swap of `imaging.cellpose_segment` to `imaging.threshold (otsu)` + `imaging.connected_components` because cellpose-SAM cannot predict on `SRSImage` voltage floats; framework-layer capability dispatch + OME propagation verified end-to-end including an in-process verify script at `scripts/verify_ome_propagation_e2e001.py`), E2E-002 is fail-with-known-blockers (the two framework bugs above fixed in-PR; final notebook execution blocked by a Windows pyzmq + Python 3.13 + jupyter incompatibility outside hotfix scope). Two follow-up issues filed and deferred: #1306 (TIFF loader ignores OME-TIFF metadata despite capability claim) and #1309 (ADR-041 CodeBlock cwd semantics contradiction between `working_directory` and exchange-folder ports — attempted fix reverted because it broke `test_codeblock_runs_python_script_through_exchange`). (@agent, 2026-05-20, branch: hotfix/adr-043-e2e-validation, session: n/a-hotfix-no-gate)

- [#1296] Phase C1 audit follow-up — four targeted fixes against the ADR-043 package-migration umbrella so spec acceptance criterion SC-003 closes end-to-end: (1) wrap the `fireEvent.change` in `frontend/src/__tests__/CapabilityDropdown.test.tsx::it("calls onChange with the picked id when user selects an option")` with an explicit `waitFor` for option visibility before firing the synthetic change event (P1-01 — the existing `await waitFor(loadCapabilities)` did not flush the post-fetch React re-render, so `select.value` was set to `""` on faster CI shards and the component's early `if (!nextId) return` guard ignored the event); (2) capture the decoded pixel buffer to a local before reassigning `img` in `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/src/scistudio_blocks_imaging/io/pillow_handler.py:_load_png` / `_load_jpeg` when the caller passes `axes_override` (P2-01 — the previous `np.asarray(img._data if hasattr(img, "_data") else [])` collapsed to `np.asarray([])` because the freshly constructed `img` had no `_data` yet, silently zeroing the buffer); (3) emit OME-XML to the TIFF `ImageDescription` tag via `ome_types.to_xml(image.meta.ome)` from `_write_tiff` and parse it back on load via a new `_ome_from_tiff` helper in `_load_tiff` (P2-05 — unblocks SC-003 end-to-end OME round-trip; the `scistudio-blocks-imaging.image.tiff.{load,save}` capabilities already advertised `format_metadata_reads=("ome",)` / `format_metadata_writes=("ome",)`); (4) rewire `SaveImage._resolve_format` and a new `_save_image_extension_map` helper to derive from `SaveImage.format_capabilities` instead of the legacy `SaveImage.supported_extensions` ClassVar (P2-03 — mirrors the A1 `save_data._legacy_save_extension_map` pattern, eliminates dual-source-of-truth drift). Adds regression tests: SC-003 end-to-end OME round-trip in `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/tests/test_format_capabilities.py::test_sc_003_ome_metadata_survives_tiff_round_trip` (gracefully skipped on Python 3.14 environments with the known `xsdata` `from_xml` parsing bug; CI on 3.11/3.13 exercises it); axes-override pixel-buffer preservation in new `packages/scistudio-blocks-imaging/tests/test_pillow_handler.py`; and `_resolve_format` derivation from `format_capabilities` plus `_save_image_extension_map` shape coverage in `test_format_capabilities.py`. - [#1355] Implement ADR-039 Addendum 1 §11.3 history-row click change: remove the row-click → `GitDiffModal` shortcut from `frontend/src/components/Git/GitHistoryList.tsx` (list view `<li>` `onClick` deleted; `role="button"` dropped; `Enter` key on a focused row no longer opens the modal) and add explicit inline `[Diff]` and `[Restore]` buttons on every row. The new `[Diff]` button reuses the same parent-SHA / empty-tree fallback that `handleRowClick` previously computed (Codex P2-B fix from PR #940 retained); the existing `[Restore this version]` button is unchanged. Both buttons `event.stopPropagation()` so they cannot bubble through to the row, and both are native `<button>` elements so they are inherently Tab-reachable. `d` / `r` hotkeys mirror the buttons on a focused list row (`d` opens diff, `r` restores). Graph view: `frontend/src/components/Git/GitGraph/interactions.ts::onCommitClick` and the `Enter`/`Space` activation in `onCommitDotKeyDown` no longer auto-open the diff — they update `focusedRow` to the clicked/activated commit (so keyboard nav has a sensible anchor) and forward to a caller-supplied `onOpenDiff` only if one is passed; the `GitHistoryList.tsx::GitGraphPane` consumer no longer supplies one, so dot click and dot Enter are focus-only by default (the diff is reached by toggling to List view and clicking `[Diff]`). `GitGraphPane`'s `onCommitClick` prop is now optional to match. The `GraphInteractionsApi.onCommitClick` JSDoc and the interactions.ts module-level docstring spell out the new semantics. Test rewrite: `frontend/src/components/Git/__tests__/GitHistoryList.test.tsx` drops the "clicking a row dispatches onCommitClick" assertion and replaces it with seven new cases — row-click is a no-op for onCommitClick / diff modal; `[Diff]` button dispatches onCommitClick when provided; `[Diff]` button opens GitDiffModal when no onCommitClick prop is supplied; `[Restore]` still dispatches onRestoreClick and stops propagation; `d` hotkey opens diff; `r` hotkey restores; `Enter` on a focused row is a no-op; both inline buttons are keyboard-reachable. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: feat/issue-1355/inline-history-row-buttons)

- [#1353 #1354] Implement ADR-039 Addendum 1 §11.3 cancellation/replacement rows: (1) remove all SciStudio git stash affordances (#1353) — delete `frontend/src/components/Git/StashListPanel.tsx`, `frontend/src/components/Git/StashApplyDialog.tsx`, the four `/api/git/stash*` endpoints in `src/scistudio/api/routes/git.py`, and the four `stash_list`/`stash_save`/`stash_apply`/`stash_drop` methods in `src/scistudio/core/versioning/git_engine.py`; strip `StashListPanel` import + Stashes button + `<StashListPanel/>` mount from `GitTab.tsx`; strip `StashApplyDialog` import + `stashPrompt` state + `status === "stashed"` branch + `<StashApplyDialog/>` mount from `GitHistoryList.tsx`; remove `stashes` field + `loadStashes` thunk + `stash_id` return-type variant from `gitSlice.ts`; remove `gitStashList`/`gitStashSave`/`gitStashApply`/`gitStashDrop` from `lib/api.ts`; remove `GitStashEntry` + `GitStashApplyResult` from `types/api.ts`; remove the amber "Your unsaved changes were stashed as ..." hint from `RunDetail.tsx`. (2) Replace dirty-tree auto-stash with auto-commit (#1354) — `git_engine.restore` no longer auto-stashes on a dirty tree (the caller is now expected to auto-commit upstream); `routes/git.py::restore` pre-checks `engine.status()["dirty"]`, calls `engine.commit(prefix="auto", message="pre-restore @ <iso-ts> (target=<short_sha>)")` first, catches `"nothing to commit"` as no-op, and returns `{status: "ok", auto_commit_sha: <sha or null>}`; `routes/git.py::branch_switch` does the same with `message="pre-switch @ <iso-ts> (from=<old>, to=<new>)"` and returns `{status, current_branch, auto_commit_sha}`. Frontend: `gitSlice.switchBranch` + `gitSlice.restore` consume the new shapes and stamp the auto-commit hint into a new `lastNotice` slot; `BranchPicker` surfaces a transient toast on auto-commit; `RunDetail.RestoreWorkflowButton` shows "Your unsaved changes were committed as <short_sha> before the restore — see History tab to revert if unintended" (the user-reported Lineage Restore confusion fix). Hotfix #997 skip-if-unchanged short-circuit in `engine.restore` retained — it correctly prevents creating empty pre-restore commits. Tests: rewritten `tests/core/test_git_engine.py::test_restore_round_trip` to assert restore-on-clean-tree round trip (auto-commit lives at the route layer now, not the engine), rewritten `tests/api/test_git_endpoints.py::test_restore_endpoint_*` + new `test_restore_endpoint_auto_commits_dirty_tree` and `test_branch_switch_auto_commits_dirty_tree` to assert the new `auto_commit_sha` payload + the `auto: pre-restore @ ...` / `auto: pre-switch @ ...` commits land on HEAD; deleted all `test_stash_*` tests in both files plus `test_stash_save_clean_409`; rewritten `test_restore_skips_when_file_unchanged` to assert HEAD stability instead of the deleted stash-count check; frontend vitest rewrites: `gitSlice.test.ts` drops the `stash_id` payload test, `GitTab.test.tsx` drops the Stashes-drawer test and asserts the button is absent, `RunDetail.restore.test.tsx` asserts the new auto-commit hint copy. PR opens against the `umbrella/adr-039-addendum-1-impl` branch (#1364, not `main`) per the manager-coordinated addendum cascade. (@agent, 2026-05-21, branch: feat/issue-1353-1354/remove-stash-add-auto-commit)

(from=..., to=...)"`); (4) cancel the §3.5 / §3.5b history-row-click-opens-modal behavior in favor of inline `[Diff]` and `[Restore]` buttons on every row; (5) surface a residual lineage-orphan bug found by the §11.2 investigation (branch delete can orphan commits referenced by `runs.workflow_git_commit`). - [#1296] Migrate in-tree `LoadData` and `SaveData` core IO blocks to explicit ADR-043 `FormatCapability` declarations (FR-001 / FR-002 / FR-015): per-(core_type, format_id) records under the `core.{type}.{format}.{load|save}` capability-id convention, `is_synthesized=False`, `is_default=True`, `pixel_only` metadata fidelity, pickle records carrying `notes='requires allow_pickle=True'`, and round-trip pairing via `roundtrip_group=core.{type}.{format}`. - [#1078] Add `engine/materialisation.py` (`materialise_to_file` / `reconstruct_from_file`) plus `utils/fs.py::mount_pathlike` cross-platform link helper (ADR-028 §D8). Module lives at the `engine/` layer rather than `core/` (planning doc said `core/`, but layer-dependency tests forbid `core/` from importing `blocks/` and the helpers must consume `BlockRegistry`; the issue title's "Engine:" prefix is the intended layer). The two new helpers consume `BlockRegistry.find_saver` / `find_loader` from #1077 to give engine + bridge code a single canonical surface for writing a `DataObject` to a file in a chosen format and constructing a typed `DataObject` from a path; AppBlock prepare/restore follow-ups (#1079 / #1080) will route through these instead of reimplementing format dispatch. `materialise_to_file` prefers a native link (`mount_pathlike`) when `obj.storage_ref` already lives on disk in the target format and falls back to a saver round-trip on link failure; `reconstruct_from_file` falls back to `Artifact(file_path=path, ...)` when no loader matches and `target_type` is an `Artifact` subclass, raises `LookupError` otherwise, and has a documented dynamic-port second-pass (`find_loader(DataObject, ext)` + `core_type` injection) so the core `LoadData` block is reachable for concrete core target types. `mount_pathlike` uses POSIX symlinks on \*nix and prefers Windows directory junctions (no admin) or NTFS hardlinks for files; raises `OSError` when no primitive succeeds. 12 new tests in `tests/core/test_materialisation.py` + 6 in `tests/utils/test_fs.py` (platform-gated symlink / junction / hardlink cases). 688 tests pass across `tests/core` + `tests/utils` + `tests/blocks/test_registry*`. (@claude, 2026-05-18, branch: fix/issue-1078/core-materialisation-helpers, session: 20260518-025336-fix-1078-core-materialisation-py-utils-f)

- [#1077] Add `BlockRegistry.find_loader(dtype, ext)`, `find_saver(dtype, ext)`, and `find_io_blocks_for_type(dtype, direction)` query methods (ADR-028 §D8). Each method consults the cached `supported_extensions` ClassVar (added on `BlockSpec` so dispatch does not require re-importing the block class) and uses `TypeSignature.matches` (ADR-027) for type compatibility — loaders are filtered by output-type-IS-A-dtype, savers by dtype-IS-A-saver-accepted-type (the classical covariance/contravariance flip). Disambiguation prefers the longest matching accepted-type chain (most specific); first-registered-wins on ties. Class resolution mirrors `instantiate()`: mtime-keyed reload for Tier-1 drop-ins, regular `import_module` otherwise; per-block import failures drop the candidate silently to match scan-loop tolerance. 17 new tests in `tests/blocks/test_registry_find.py` covering exact match, subtype direction (both polarities), specificity ordering, first-registered tie-break, case-insensitivity, `dtype=None` shortcut, enumeration order, and invalid-direction error. Full registry suite (77) + architecture suite (273) green. (@claude, 2026-05-18, branch: fix/issue-1077/blockregistry-find-loader-saver, session: 20260518-021831-fix-1077-blockregistry-find-loader-find)
